{"uri": "2024-07-438724712", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-30", "time": "19:48:42", "dateTime": "2024-07-30T19:48:42Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-30T19:20:04Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8705882430076599, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-london-issues-fix-creators-promise/", "title": "Fallout: London Creators Promise Fixes to Mod's Biggest Issues Soon", "body": "Highlights\n\nFallout: London devs promise to fix game-breaking issues soon, thanking the community for its support. The Fallout 4 mod has been praised for its story and world-building, but is plagued with crashes affecting gameplay.\n\nThe creators of the Fallout 4 total conversion mod Fallout: London have promised to fix the game's \"reported technical issues\" soon. While this Fallout 4 mod was recently released with mostly positive acclaim from fans, it currently has several game-breaking issues, effectively preventing some people from playing it.\n\nOriginally announced by the non-profit modding group Team FOLON in 2021, Fallout: London was recently released on GOG. The mod is entirely free, but it was released on the store because its files were too big for other modding platforms such as Nexus Mods. Despite being praised for its story and world-building, however, many gamers experienced constant crashes when they started playing Fallout: London.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout London: Where to Find Dove's Dilemma (Catching Up Quest Guide)\n\nThe Sidequest \"Catching Up\" has players tracking down books to help Sabertooth Syd learn his letters, but one book can be troublesome to find.\n\nNow, Team FOLON has thanked the community for their support and promised to fix the reported technical issues currently plaguing Fallout: London. While the team did not give an official date for an update, Team FOLON claims that the patch will come out \"soon.\" In the meantime, gamers should carefully read the installation instructions of the game before installing it to avoid compatibility issues. The use of Fallout 4's Buffout 4 mod is also indicated to diminish crashes.\n\nTeam FOLON Promises to Solve Fallout: London's Technical Issues\n\nAt the moment, Fallout: London has a score of 3.3/5 on GOG. While it still has many positive reviews, considering it's a huge and complex mod made by a non-profit group, the score is likely affected by the many issues gamers had while playing it. It's easy to find multiple comments on the game's page stating that Fallout: London crashes all the time, essentially making it unplayable for a significant portion of the user base.\n\nClose\n\nPC gamers who want to try out Fallout: London can do it if they currently have GOG or Steam copies of Fallout 4. Due to the need to downgrade Fallout 4's version for the mod to work, the Epic Games Store of Fallout 4 is not compatible with Fallout: London, as the EGS platform does not give players that option.\n\nUnfortunately, there are still no updates from Team FOLON regarding a console release of Fallout: London. Team FOLON has previously confirmed that Fallout: London won't be available for consoles, as its files are too big to be allowed on the console modding platforms, the same problem that prevented the game from being on Nexus Mods. If Bethesda's owner, Microsoft, would make an exception for the game, this could be possible, but gamers should not hold their breaths, as it's unlikely that this would happen.\n\nFallout 4\n\nFallout 4 is an RPG in the Fallout series, being the fourth major installment. {"uri": "2024-07-435636627", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-27", "time": "19:16:49", "dateTime": "2024-07-27T19:16:49Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-27T19:00:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8392156958580017, "url": "https://screenrant.com/fallout-london-setting-british-factions-locations-england/", "title": "Fallout: London Understands Why The Series' Settings Are So Important", "body": "Rare Fallout 4 Glitch Gives Players Full View Of An In-Game Myth With Real-World Inspiration\n\nSummary\n\nSettings play a crucial role in Fallout games, influencing factions & creating unique atmospheres. Fallout: London mod captures the British essence with landmarks, accents, & factions like Knights of Camelot. Modding, like with Fallout: London , showcases the robustness of Bethesda's Creation Kit, allowing for total conversion mods.\n\nBethesda has always ensured that the settings of Fallout games have had a strong influence on the title that uses them, and the mod authors of Fallout: London understand this well. Whether it be the Mojave Desert of New Vegas or the Boston area of Fallout 4, each title in the series has a distinct feeling, specific factions, and recognizable landmarks from each of its settings. Without this, there wouldn't be a strong feeling of something brand new whenever another Fallout is released, and Fallout: London does this well enough to feel like a proper spin-off sequel.\n\nAlthough Bethesda is likely to keep the Fallout franchise within the US, even though it has expanded onto the silver screen, modders have decided to take the series abroad, using Fallout 4 as a base. Fallout: London is exactly what people would expect when they hear the name. The series has made it across the pond to England, specifically to its capital, where players of the mod can enjoy everything British while surviving the irradiated wasteland they all know and love from Fallout. It is a total conversion of Fallout 4 and is only available on PC.\n\nRelated\n\n10 Fun Fallout 4 Easter Eggs You Might Have Missed\n\nFallout 4 is jam-packed with references to movies, TV shows, literature, and other games for players to find with these being some of the best.\n\nSettings Are Pivotal To Each Fallout Game\n\nFactions & Storylines Depend On Them\n\nClose\n\nThe settings of Fallout games have always been an underrated part of the titles. Usually, players focus on the many, many Vaults and their experiments or the longstanding factions everyone knows and loves, like the zealous Brotherhood of Steel, but visiting famous landmarks of specific cities has always been a part of Fallout's DNA. Without it, there wouldn't be the added context of what was lost when the bombs were dropped and when the world was turned into an apocalyptic wasteland filled with irradiated cockroaches and feral Deathclaws.\n\nSettings also inform what kind of factions a Vault Dweller (or Courier) can expect when venturing out into the world. With the Mojave being in California, New Vegas made sure to give the NCR a big role in the game, with them previously appearing in Fallout 2. Caesar's Legion was made to be in conflict with the NCR, while Mr House (a play on the house always wins) was made as the ruler of New Vegas. This isn't the only game that lets its setting influence the factions and major players, as Fallout 4 did, too.\n\nMr House makes an appearance in the Fallout series. There, he's known as Robert House and is in charge of RobCo Industries.\n\nAlthough mentioned before, the Institute is a major player in Fallout 4 and was founded by surviving students of the Commonwealth Institute of Technology (C.I.T), which is Fallout's equivalent of M.I.T. The university's famed knowledge of science and technology in real life influenced the Institute, and from that, the Railroad was founded in opposition. Fallout 4 also introduced the Commonwealth Minutemen, who used Fort Independence as a base, which they later called The Castle.\n\nFallout: London Is So Delightfully British\n\nBrings London To Life\n\nArguably, the mod team behind Fallout: London takes the use of its setting even further than prior titles in the series. Everything from locations, clothing, and dog breeds has been influenced by London, with some characters wearing the Union Jack on jackets and having the punk aesthetic that took Britain by storm in the 70s. German Shepherds have been replaced by the mighty Bulldog, while players can visit landmarks like St Paul's Cathedral and the Millennium Wheel.\n\nThe Millennium Wheel was made to celebrate the millennium and is also known as the London Eye.\n\nThe mod authors have gone the extra mile with accents, too, ensuring that the many, many regional accents of London have been lovingly captured by a capable voice cast, with Lambeth being home to many with a cockney accent, for instance. The iconic Big Ben and the Elizabeth tower are present, as well as streets filled with ruined, red, double-decker buses. Even the London Underground's Tube Network has been lovingly recreated, with the tubes actually racing through the stations.\n\nMuch like other Fallout games, the factions have been influenced by the setting, too. One of Britain's most famous legends revolves around King Arthur and Camelot, so the developers took this legend and created the Knights of Camelot faction, complete with a round table and all. There are also the Vagabonds (based on British gangs like the Peaky Blinders), the Gentry (based on the British aristocracy), and Tommies, who are based on WW1 soldiers. Tommies got their name because many English soldiers were called Tommy.\n\nRelated\n\nIngenious Fallout 4 Build Makes Sure The Sole Survivor Will Never Run Out Of Ammo\n\nA Fallout 4 player has created an impressive new build that ensures they will never run out of ammo again.\n\nFallout: London Proves Modding Is Bigger Than Ever\n\nTotal Conversion Mods Are Becoming The Norm\n\nWith the level of freedom that the Creation Kit for its games provides, Bethesda has ensured that its titles can last far longer than other single-player titles just because there is a constant stream of content flowing to them. Fallout: London is a well-researched, lovingly made passion project the size of a full game, but it is not the only one made for a Bethesda title. Enderal: Forgotten Stories, a total conversion for Skyrim, is another example and shows that the Creation Kit gives players the tools as long as they bring the passion.\n\nThe Creation Kit is a modding tool made for Bethesda games, like Skyrim and Fallout 4, which uses the Creation Engine.\n\nWith references to both British history, particularly WW1 with the Tommies and WW2 with hanging Spitfire fighters, and folklore with the Camelot faction, this shows that the mod isn't just surface level when it comes to using its setting. Much like previous Fallout titles, landmarks haven't just been recreated, the areas have also been cleverly used too. Fallout: London uses the Thames River to create the shanty town-like settlement of Thameshaven and St Paul's Cathedral to make St Paul's Sanctuary, similar to Diamond City in Fallout 4.\n\nA game's setting will always be important in informing what developers can use to make their title feel more immersive. Fallout: London has followed in the footsteps of prior titles in the series by putting its setting center stage and allowing it to not only give players memorable landmarks to visit but also inform what factions are present. The way the setting has been used has made the mod both a brilliant tribute to the Fallout franchise and a creative love letter to London and all things British.\n\nSource: {"uri": "8247753981", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-28", "time": "18:01:50", "dateTime": "2024-07-28T18:01:50Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-28T18:01:16Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8039215803146362, "url": "https://gamingbolt.com/everything-you-need-to-know-about-fallout-london", "title": "Everything You Need to Know About Fallout London", "body": "Here's everything you should know about this long-awaited total conversion mod.\n\nWith Bethesda Game Studios busy with Starfield post-launch content and the development of The Elder Scrolls 6, the chances of us getting a new Fallout game in the next few years are slim to none, but those looking for a new Fallout fix do have a solid alternative to turn to. Fallout 4's expansion sized total conversion mod, Fallout London, has been in development and making waves for years, and now, it is finally out, allowing players to dive into a huge, entirely new, if unofficial, Fallout journey. Here, we're going to go over all the key details that you should know about it.\n\nSTORY\n\nBeing an unofficial mod, Fallout London is obviously not going to be part of the series' canon, but it is promising to tell an interesting story. The game is set in the year 2237, which puts it between the events of Fallout 1 and 2, and roughly 50 years before the events of Fallout 4. What makes it particularly interesting, however, is the fact that, as its name gives away, it's set in London. Never in the history of the Fallout franchise have we stepped outside of the United States of America, so it should be interesting to see what Fallout London's take on the post-apocalyptic remains of the English city are. From a narrative perspective, the mod focuses on several factions vying for control over London- but more on that in a bit. For now, let's speak about London itself.\n\nMAP DETAILS\n\nBeing able to explore the post-nuclear remains of the city of London in Fallout's post-apocalyptic world is obviously one of the bigger draws of this mod, but what exactly can we expect from the map? According to the development team, Team FOLON, the mod's map is going to be quite a sizeable one- as large as the map of Fallout 4's base game and its Far Harbor DLC put together, in fact, which, if you've played those two, sounds like a huge play area. In total, the map is divided into 15 boroughs, and according to Team FOLON, there's as much as 90 hours of content for players to get through.\n\nFallout: London is looking to leverage its London setting in some truly interesting ways- including giving us a glimpse into an alternative reality where we could see what a Fallout game set outside of the USA and the series' focus on Americana-driven satire would look like. According to Team FOLON, you can expect plenty of elements that are usually staples of the franchise to be MIA in this game. For starters, in the Fallout lore the Forced Evolutionary Virus (or FEV) never made its way to London, which means all of the monstrosities and nightmarish creatures it created won't be in the mod either. That includes Super Mutants and Deathclaws, among other things. Additionally, you can also expect Vault-Tec to have no presence in London whatsoever, since it's an American company- though you can expect other, dingier underground vaults.\n\nWEAPONS\n\nAnother area where it looks like Fallout London is attempting to deliver a different kind of Fallout experience is the combat, which, according to Team FOLON, is going to be much less focused on gunplay. Instead, players can expect melee weapons to play a much larger role, to the extent of being the only weapons you'll be using at times. Gunplay has admittedly never been one of Fallout's strengths, but the shooting did see significant improvements in Fallout 4 over previous titles, so it should be interesting to see how Fallout London fares with its combat changes.\n\nFactions have always played a huge role in any Fallout experience (or any Bethesda Game Studios RPG, for that matter), and yes, there will be plenty of those that players will be crossing paths with in Fallout: London as well. The most powerful of them all is the Gentry, who are the current rulers of London and descendants of the pre-war aristocracy and government, who are looking to rebuild the United Kingdom once more. Then there are the Tommies, a militia that has become a tool for the Gentry; 5th Column, an anarchist faction looking to tear down the established rule in London in order to rebuild a new empire; and the Camelot Republic, an underground resistance movement that is also looking to remove the Gentry from power and instead replace them with a new representative republic government.\n\nMORE FACTIONS\n\nYes, there are still more factions to talk about- London is a big place after all, and there's plenty of different groups with their own motivations and goals that you'll be working with and against. There's the Isle of Dogs Syndicate, for instance, which is essentially a gang in control of Millwall that runs a sizeable smuggling operation. There are the Vagabonds, who are described as the mortal enemies of the aforementioned Ise of Dogs Syndicate, and are on a quest for revenge. There's also the elusive and mysterious group known as Angel, rumoured to be descendants of a secret pre-war science ministry who have eyes all over the city. In total, Team FOLON says there are 20 factions\n\nLike the series that it owes its existence to, Fallout London is also going to feature a number of different companion characters that players will be able to meet, recruit, and head out on quests with. In total, there are going to be seven companion characters, each of whom will bring their own story tidbits and ties to different factions.\n\nDIALOGUE\n\nFallout: London may be a mod based on Fallout 4, but it's looking to tweak the base gameplay experience in some notable ways. For instance, the base game's dialogue system has been expanded for the mod, with Team FOLON promising an experience that places choice and consequence mechanics front and center, something that Fallout 4 was criticized for not doing. Additionally, the development team has also confirmed that the main protagonist in the mod isn't voiced, which is another area where the base game drew criticism. Additionally, speaking of voice acting, though the protagonist is going to be a silent one, all major characters in Fallout: London will be fully voiced.\n\nSeveral other finer details have also been revealed on Fallout London. For instance, settlements - a core component of the Fallout 4 base game - is going to be part of the experience here as well, with a total of seven new and unique settlements included in the mod. In addition to that, players can expect dynamic new animations, new craftable items, new weapons to use in combat, as many as 200 quests, and more. Oh, and for those of you wondering whether Fallout London is ever going to show up on consoles- Team FOLON says the mod is going to be available only on PC. Will that possibly change in the future? Never say never, I guess, but that's not the plan right, at least.\n\nREQUIREMENTS\n\nTo be able to access Fallout London, you're going to need not just the Fallout 4 base game, but also all of its DLC (which means you could also just buy the Game of the Year Edition). Available via both Steam and GoG, the mod will also need you to disable cloud saves, and will replace the actual, official game entirely. If you want to get the game back, you'll have to uninstall it and the mod, before reinstalling the former again.", "source": {"uri": "gamingbolt.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "GamingBolt"}, {"uri": "2024-07-438115863", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-30", "time": "10:08:47", "dateTime": "2024-07-30T10:08:47Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-30T10:00:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7882353067398071, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-spin-off-larian-studios-baldurs-gate-3-spin-off/", "title": "One Award-Winning Studio is a Clear Contender for a Fallout Spin-Off", "body": "With Bethesda recently releasing Starfield and locking its sights on The Elder Scrolls 6, it could be a while before gaming audiences get their hands on another entry in the Fallout series. At the same time, the success of Amazon's Fallout TV series, combined with the almost decade-long lapse between releases, means that demand for a new Fallout is greater than ever. In light of these facts, it may be in Bethesda's best interest to outsource the IP.\n\nIt wouldn't be the first time the company has done something like this. 2010's Fallout: New Vegas, which is often considered the best entry in the series, was not developed by Bethesda Game Studios, the team behind Fallout 3 and eventually Fallout 4. Instead, it came from Obsidian Entertainment, and this fresh set of minds allowed New Vegas to experiment with several role-playing elements that BGS either didn't consider or decided not to implement in its first Fallout game, ultimately leading to a more distinct and original final product. Bethesda could do this again, and there's one beloved studio that would be the perfect candidate.\n\n1:36\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 5 Can Step Up Its Building Game By Following Starfield's Lead\n\nOne highly creative feature from Bethesda's sci-fi adventure Starfield has every reason to find its way into the developer's next Fallout game.\n\nBethesda Should Hand Larian Studios the Reins to Fallout\n\nClose\n\nLarian's RPG Chops Could Make for a Great Fallout Experience\n\nLarian Studios, the company behind the awards-dominating Baldur's Gate 3, has done more than enough to establish itself as a powerful force in the CRPG space. BG3 itself is seen by many as the pinnacle of the studio's prowess, as it provides a deep, dizzyingly complex role-playing adventure, characterized by countless layers of decision-making and multifaceted build variety. Indeed, Baldur's Gate 3 is a triumph within the RPG genre, and it's clear that Larian still has more gas in the tank.\n\nThough BG3 catapulted the studio into the mainstream, Larian had already found respect among CRPG fans with the Divinity: Original Sin games years prior.\n\nThough BG3 is a high-fantasy story set in the Dungeons and Dragons universe, there's no reason why Larian couldn't take a crack at a game in a more modern or post-apocalyptic setting like Fallout's. Interestingly enough, Larian Studios boss Swen Vincke went on record saying that the company was eyeing the Fallout license ahead of Baldur's Gate 3, which demonstrates, if not a commitment to the property, at least an openness to working on it. Larian bringing its talents, specifically its emphasis on narrative and player choice, to Fallout could lead to incredible results.\n\nLarian Studios Could Bring Fallout Back to Its Roots\n\nWhile modern gaming audiences may associate Fallout with the FPS gameplay established with Fallout 3, the franchise was once defined by a very different sort of formula. The first two Fallout games were turn-based CRPGs with a top-down perspective, not too unlike Baldur's Gate 3. Of course, BG3 is a more advanced, complex, and modernized version of this more rudimentary formula, but it maintains the genre's top priorities, which include narrative, character choice, exploration, and an abundance of dialog.\n\nThe modern, post-Bethesda-acquisition Fallout games, while they certainly have their own unique strengths, adopt more of an action-RPG framework, where combat and overwhelming scale reign supreme.\n\nThis can lead to an immersive and atmospheric experience, as activities like roaming the vast expanses of the Capital Wasteland are valuable in their own right, but it also means that the tabletop-derived RPG mechanics take a back seat. This stands in stark contrast to the older Fallout games and Baldur's Gate 3, which draw heavily from Dungeons and Dragons and other tabletop games to offer a tighter, more methodical, and more flexible role-playing experience.\n\nOf course, Larian is working on its own projects, so it may not be able to pick up a BG3-style Fallout spin-off, even if Bethesda was willing to share the license. Plus, it's hard to say if Larian even wants to stick to the BG3 formula for future games. {"uri": "2024-07-436271151", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-28", "time": "15:54:02", "dateTime": "2024-07-28T15:54:02Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-28T15:32:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7843137383460999, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-fallout-5-protagonist-new-vegas-similiar-good-why/", "title": "Fallout 5's Protagonist Should Be More New Vegas and Less Bethesda", "body": "Fallout has given gamers what is likely the most iconic depiction of a post-apocalyptic nuclear setting in the entire medium, and perhaps even beyond. Over the course of its releases, Fallout has built and established one of the most engrossing worlds through its characters and locations, creating a foundational world that personifies what many imagine when invoking the image of a nuclear war that ravaged the Earth. Reaching back to the 1997 original, players usually start off as a Vault Dweller, one of the inhabitants of the underground bunkers constructed to withstand the bombs dropping on the surface.\n\nAfter the IP passed to Bethesda Game Studios, the tradition was rigidly adhered to. While this framework is effective for introducing and immersing fans at the beginning of each game, it's also becoming somewhat predictable. Even the recent popular Fallout Amazon TV series positioned its protagonist, Lucy MacLean, as a fresh-faced Vault resident thrust into the Wasteland. Though it's practical for the studio to utilize this device, as it caters to both longtime fans and newcomers, there are solid arguments to be made for Bethesda to look to Obsidian Entertainment's vision for Fallout: New Vegas' non-Vault Dweller protagonist for the fifth numbered entry in the franchise.\n\nFallout 76 will offer playable ghoul characters in an update set to arrive next year.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout: All Player Character Origins, Ranked\n\nEach protagonist in the Fallout series has an origin story that explains their motive for exploring the Wasteland, but which is the most iconic?\n\nFallout 5's Protagonist Should Channel New Vegas' Courier Over Bethesda's Vault Dwellers\n\nClose\n\nBethesda's Fallout Vault Dweller Protagonists May Be Getting a Little Stale\n\nBreaking down the origins of each protagonist from the mainline titles:\n\nGame\n\nProtagonist Role/Title\n\nPlace of Origin\n\nFallout 1\n\nVault Dweller\n\nVault 13\n\nFallout 2\n\nChosen One/Vault Descendant\n\nArroyo\n\nFallout 3\n\nLone Wanderer\n\nVault 101\n\nFallout: New Vegas\n\nMojave Express Courier Six\n\nUnknown (Mojave Wasteland)\n\nFallout 4\n\nSole Survivor\n\nVault 111\n\nFallout 76\n\nVarious\n\nVault 76\n\nNotably, in the Bethesda-produced titles (Fallout 3, 4, and 76), all hail from a Vault, and are rooted in the viewpoint that is attached. As Fallout 76 is an MMO, the specifics of the characters are looser to allow fans to role-play and decide their own place in the Wasteland. Nevertheless, lore states that they all originated in the titular vault, and thus every character falls under the same banner in this regard.\n\nThe major exceptions are the second title, where the main character is actually the grandchild of Fallout 1's Vault Dweller, and New Vegas. The latter's mysterious Courier, whose backstory remains largely undefined and unexplained, makes them one of the best and most unique Fallout protagonists featured so far.\n\nFallout: New Vegas' Courier was a Much-Needed Breath of Fresh Air, and Fallout 5 Should Take Note\n\nFallout: New Vegas is widely credited with being truer to the nature of the series in many ways, particularly its storytelling and RPG elements, and the Courier breaking from the tradition of Bethesda's titles also sets it apart. The Courier is central to the machinations of the major Mojave players, Mr. House, the New California Republic, and Caesar's Legion, and provides a much different window for fans to experience the plot.\n\nBethesda then could consider thinking outside the bounds of its previous protagonist conventions for Fallout 5, and look to emulate the intriguing possibilities allowed by no longer restricting its protagonist to starting off as a Vault Dweller, ala the Courier in New Vegas. This would free up avenues for the narrative and upend expectations in the process, making Fallout's Vaults alien and intimidating (even more so than usual) to a character who has not been born and raised in one.\n\nA bigger stretch might be to offer either option, though this would likely impact the plot to such a degree that it may not be reasonably feasible. Still, having a main character begin from the viewpoint of a native Wastelander or another outsider like the Courier versus a Vault resident could inject a lot of fresh perspective into the next game.\n\nFallout 4\n\nFallout 4 is an RPG in the Fallout series, being the fourth major installment. Many jumped back in and were pleasantly surprised by the attention to detail in the world, the gunplay, the secrets and the companions. However, there was still plenty of criticism for its story, the decision to go with a voiced protagonist, lackluster role-playing mechanics, the endings and much more. There was still that feeling, especially among some longtime fans of the franchise, that it just didn't feel like a Fallout game (which is saying something considering some players lobbied those same criticisms against Fallout 3).\n\nThe fervor may have died down, and each title has dropped back down to more conservative player numbers - though Fallout 4 continues to see enthusiasm following its Next-Gen Update - but there's a new Fallout experience in town. In development since 2019, Fallout: London is a mod for Fallout 4 that's more like a total conversion. Though it seemed like it wouldn't arrive on Steam due to the Next-Gen Update breaking several things, it's finally available for PC players.\n\nThere are some very mixed results with the installation (long story short: Use the GOG version), and performance leaves a lot to be desired. Nevertheless, it's an experience that's proven delightfully surprising to the extent that fans of the franchise owe it to themselves to play, if not try it out.\n\nThe name indicates the basic premise. What if players ventured out into the post-apocalyptic nuclear wasteland of London? The series has predominantly focused on the United States of America, allowing for pop culture references and commentary on consumerism. It's the first time players can see how another part of the world has been affected by the bombs dropping, unofficial as it is.\n\nThere's no Vault-Tec - no Super Mutants, Deathclaws or other elements that will be familiar to longtime fans because, well, the Forced Evolutionary Virus never made its way across the ocean. While that may sound disappointing, it also means you have to adapt to new threats. Furthermore, it unfolds in 2237 between Fallout 1 and 2. The vibe is also completely different from Fallout 4 - goodbye Sole Survivor seeking revenge for their partner and looking for Shaun. Hello silent, amnesiac protagonist who's the subject of an unknown experiment.\n\nYou awaken in a containment tube with two scientists commenting on your progress under the mysterious individual named Mr. Smythe. When the Vagabonds, one of the many factions roaming post-nuclear London, break in and start firing, you're set free. You have time to try and process what this strange facility is about, fighting off Ratshrews (a substitute for Molerats) and scrounging for supplies. As you escape, Mr. Smythe is seemingly pleased with your choice, encouraging you to venture forth. A hop, skip, and jump onto the Tube - which subsequently crashes, a fitting metaphor for this mod - and the world opens up.\n\nIt really can't be understated just how different London feels from the Commonwealth. Propaganda posts against the Brotherhood of Steel abound. Nameplates indicating where historical figures once resided are visible on the buildings. Nuka Cola is in short supply compared to tea. The Reliant Robin, or its remains, can be discovered alongside other vehicles. The attention to detail is on another level and goes a long way towards making the experience feel like more than a reskinned Fallout 4.\n\nThe fundamental gameplay is also very different. Guns aren't as commonplace, with the team focusing more on melee combat and getting up close and personal. A more dangerous approach and the base difficulty being higher than Fallout 4 means things hurt a lot more. Feral Ghouls may still seem like stumbling horrors, but a single clean hit can fracture your limbs.\n\nPicking your battles, knowing when to use firearms and backing off lest things get ugly isn't just essential in the early going - it's mandatory. This doesn't necessarily mean that you'll fight only with melee weapons throughout the entire experience. It emphasizes the despair of trying to survive with the bare essentials, slowly clawing your way up.\n\nPerhaps the biggest improvement over the base Fallout 4 experience is making decisions matter. You could join the Vagabonds and partake in different tasks, leading to multiple quests and choices (while obtaining a sweet Butterfly Knife). Alternatively, you could visit the Thamesfolk and learn more about the mysterious facility and potentially who the Gentry are.\n\nMaybe you want to forego both choices and explore the world unfettered. It's ultimately up to you, and while the impact of each decision has yet to be fully revealed, they feel significant. You have skill checks that range from getting some water from the Vagabonds and potentially saving someone's life (or making their condition worse) to heavier choices deciding whether to disrupt a supply line.\n\nWhile developer Team FOLON calls this a \"condensed\" version of London, covering 15 boroughs (roughly half of the real-world city), the map size is the equivalent of the Commonwealth and Far Harbor from Fallout 4. Also, while touting this as a DLC-sized mod, it has 200 quests and promises 90 hours of gameplay. It's like a whole new game - granted, one built on an existing game's foundation, but still offering boatloads of new content for players to experience.\n\nThe developer outlines various factions from the rebellious 5th Column to the militaristic Tommies and the Knights of the Round-inspired Camelot. You may even encounter Mr. Smythe's mysterious organization. They all seem to have dedicated questlines, but the kicker is that they're only a small percentage - TEAM FOLON lists 20 factions with varying story paths and endings. The fact that all of this is free is simply mind-boggling.\n\nSo it's a shame that it's not the most optimized mod out there. Players who install through GOG report crashes after roughly an hour of play. Some don't even get that far, suffering consecutive crashes in the process, even with officially recommended mods like Buffout 4. These will naturally be worked on, but many fixes may not roll out immediately, leading to frustration.\n\nThe installation experience on Steam is also much more challenging - at least GOG has heavily discounted Fallout 4: Game of the Year Edition to lower the barrier of entry. It's also worth noting that your mileage may vary with the quality of the voice acting, which can feel impressive at times and flat during others. However, the cameos, which we won't spoil, are excellent.\n\nDespite its optimization issues, one can't overstate enough just how incredible this mod is, especially from an independent team that's spread worldwide. Even if it's been in development for the past five years, the sheer quality of the experience, from its rendition of London and depiction of British culture, is still hard to believe. It once again speaks volumes of the modding community for Bethesda titles and what they're capable of achieving, be it much-needed fixes or fresh new experiences that can rival the base game in many ways.\n\nWhile it may not overhaul every element, Fallout: London is well worth looking into, whether you're seeking something far meatier beyond the current assortment of mods, are a fan of the series or just curious what the buzz is about. Set in a world that barely survived a nuclear apocalypse, the Fallout franchise's vaults are one of its most recognizable features, but life isn't what the residents expected in most of them.\n\nPlayers took their first steps in the series in Fallout's Vault 13, the starting location of the original PC game, and other than a malfunctioning water chip with no backup to be found, life seemed pretty normal there. {"uri": "2024-07-435680869", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-27", "time": "20:56:42", "dateTime": "2024-07-27T20:56:42Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-27T20:30:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6705882549285889, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-76-mole-miners-dark-lore-radiation-mutation-humanity/", "title": "Fallout 76's Mole Miners Hold Some Dark Implications for Future Series Enemies", "body": "The Fallout series' depiction of a post-nuclear wasteland is filled with terrifying and grotesque creatures mutated by exposure to immense radiation. While iconic enemies like ghouls or deathclaws stand out as some of the best-designed enemies in the series, Fallout 76 has its own additions to the universe's monster compendium that rival the likes of these creatures. One of the most notable enemies added in Fallout 76 is the mole miner, whose disturbing origins should lay the foundation for future Fallout enemies to expand upon.\n\nFallout 76 has proven to be a goldmine of potential when it comes to expanding the universe of Fallout with more unique enemy types. While the game boasts several cryptids native to its Appalachian setting, such as the Mothman or the Flatwoods Monster, it also plays to its setting's strengths when it comes to more common enemies as well. The mole miners are the perfect depiction of West Virginia's mining industry gone wrong when a nuclear apocalypse hits, causing a dangerous profession to become the origin of some of Fallout's darkest lore.\n\nRelated\n\nUpcoming Fallout 76 Feature Shows How Far Fallout 4's Base Building Has Come\n\nA new feature scheduled to come to Fallout 76 in the Milepost Zero update is a testament to the growing appreciation for the game's base building.\n\nFallout 76's Mole Miners Suggests Future Enemies Could Share a Dark Trait\n\nClose\n\nAccording to the lore of Fallout 76, mole miners are mutated West Virginian miners who have become trapped within their mining suits due to the severity of their mutations. These beings are native to the Ash Heap region, where the bulk of Appalachia's mines can be found. While the mutations that have caused the mole miners to be imprisoned in their mining gear appear to be causing them a great deal of suffering, it's also allowed them to develop claws and a stout, hunched posture that allows them to wield heavy weapons ranging from shotguns to missile launchers.\n\nNot only is it a dark thought to consider that mole miners were once humans that have become trapped within their mining suits, but unlike feral ghouls, these mole miners still appear to retain a portion of their humanity. Mole miners still seem to retain the hierarchy of their former selves, with foremen and supervisors leading packs of the enemies, and an NPC like Purveyor Murmrgh showing that some are still capable of socializing with humans. These traits make it all the more tragic when realizing they are unable to breathe properly without a respirator, as well as when players are forced to kill them.\n\nFuture Fallout Enemies Should Take Notes from 76's Mole Miners\n\nIt's easy for players to mindlessly mow down feral ghouls or take out a camp of raiders since Fallout presents its world as one where it's kill or be killed. However, as the series evolves and expands its lore, injecting bits of humanity into certain enemy types adds a layer of complexity that might make players hesitate about killing them. Mole miners are a perfect example of this idea, since on the surface they appear to be a mindless, hostile force like any other feral ghoul or radroach.\n\nWhen players dig a little deeper into the lore of mole miners, they become much more tragic enemies that have clearly lost control of their actions yet still retain their humanity to some degree. Future Fallout games should try to develop more complex enemies like this, potentially using a similar design premise of a human who was so severely mutated by radiation that they are no longer in control of themselves yet still display characteristics of their former humanity. While this may be a dark route for the series to take, it could support future changes that allow players to approach the series' RPG mechanics from a pacifist playstyle.\n\nFallout Fallout's success is further proved by the fact that it was nominated for two major Emmy Awards.\n\nThe adaptation perfectly represents the franchise's satirical post-apocalyptic nature, alongside its intriguing story, dark humor, unique characters, and so forth. Furthermore, countless neat details from the games are found everywhere throughout the show's first season, ensuring seamless connections between each entry to the Fallout franchise, and respecting the lore of the games whilst expanding upon it. These details help to make this show such a great adaptation and make it worthy of appreciation by fans.\n\n10 Lucy's S.P.E.C.I.A.L. Stats\n\nRelated\n\nThis Underrated Action RPG is Perfect For Fallout Fans\n\nFallout fans wanting new content need look no further than Obsidian's 2019 open-world action game The Outer Worlds to scratch that Fallout itch.\n\nFallout's first episode introduces us to protagonist Lucy, a Vault Dweller from Vault 33 who is about to get married to Dweller Monty from Vault 32. As Lucy introduces herself to the viewer and interviews for her marriage application to the Vault 33 council, she lists her multiple different skills and how good she is in each one. The skills she mentions are strikingly similar to perks that players must choose from the S.P.E.C.I.A.L. system, like speech and science skills.\n\nThis is the very first time viewers meet Lucy, which makes this detail even better, as it is at the beginning of each recent Fallout game that players must spend their starting skill points on the S.P.E.C.I.A.L. system. This is a great callback to the Fallout games and already demonstrates the show's dedication to the lore and respect for the game mechanics, which make Fallout so unique and a fan-favorite franchise.\n\n9 Lucy Drinks Radiated Water\n\nEpisode 4 'The Ghoul' sees Lucy held hostage by Walter Goggin's the Ghoul, as they travel through the Wasteland's California ruins. Throughout the episode, Lucy fights the urge to drink radiated water despite her immense thirst and the Ghoul's purposeful waste of water. With every water source they encounter, Lucy's Pip Boy' Geiger counter warns of radiation -- but eventually, she gives in, and drinks the radiated water.\n\nThe Ghoul taunts her, warning she will mutate like him, and that she is finally learning the ways of the Wasteland. This is an interesting detail that hits too close to home for Fallout players, as every gamer who has ventured across the Wasteland will have had to have drank radiated water and other radiated drinks -- and become infected with rads. Once again this is a great detail that demonstrates how much love and respect the show has for the games.\n\n8 How Ghouls Work\n\nRelated\n\nThe Fallout Games and This Rockstar Franchise Share Some Key Similarities\n\nThese two franchises look completely different, yet both give players immense potential for freedom in exploring the most detailed worlds.\n\nFallout star Walton Goggins brought the Ghoul to life in the show, as he quickly became a fan-favorite character as a rival to Lucy. The Ghoul needs to inhale an unknown chem every so often to prevent his radiation from turning him feral like the ghouls imprisoned at the organ farm Lucy is given to. Viewers also see a ghoul turning feral in an abandoned building, demonstrating the horrifying transformation the Ghoul would go through without the chem.\n\nThe way ghouls mutate and transform into feral ghouls in the show is incredibly similar to how the series shows it, with ghouls eventually losing their minds and becoming feral. Furthermore, the genetic modifications to ghouls' bodies potentially lead to centuries-long life spans, also demonstrated in the show by the Ghoul's backstory, which revealed he had been around long before the bombs dropped. The consistency between the show and the games helps the franchise thrive, as game lore and logic are shared.\n\n7 The Show's Clothing And Weapons Are Taken Straight From The Games\n\nClose\n\nAccurate costumes in adaptations of any pop culture, such as comic-accurate costumes in Marvel movies, are a great thing, and the same is true for Fallout. The Vault Dweller outfit is a perfect example of source-accurate outfits, as they are strikingly similar to those worn throughout the games, and simply add to its immersion. Furthermore, game-accurate weapons, such as the 10mm pistol, long barrel assault rifle, and AER9 laser pistol simply further connect the show to the games.\n\nAlthough seemingly unimportant, weapons and clothing taken from the games that are present in the show help to keep consistency and the overall Fallout lore intact. Further examples of this are the game-accurate Power Armour that Maximus wears and the leather armor that Lucy wears, acting both as fan service and respect for the franchise. They are neat details that just add to the reasons why Fallout is such an incredible adaptation.\n\n6 The Broken Water Chip\n\nRelated\n\nWhy Fallout Fans Want this Terrifying Creature in Season 2\n\nDeathclaws are a much loved part of the Fallout franchise, but they have yet to make an appearance in the TV show.\n\nA fantastic detail that truly cements the adaptation as a worthy component of the Fallout franchise is a callback to the very first game in 1997, in which Vault 33's water chip is broken. In the original Fallout game, this is the beginning of the game's story, and the Vault Dweller is chosen by the Overseer to venture to the Wasteland and locate a new one.\n\nAlthough this is not the reason Lucy leaves the vault, it is a fun detail nonetheless. It demonstrates the show's respect for the franchise, even from the games developed before Bethesda took over. Furthermore, it keeps the overall narrative of the Fallout world flowing, ensuring no plotholes or overused plot points.\n\n5 Mr. Handy's Representation In The Show Is Perfect\n\nThroughout the Fallout games, Mr. Handy bots can be found programmed for different roles across the Wasteland, with the once-peaceful robots having been manipulated for more devious purposes post-war, or having malfunctioned. Not only do fans see a great version of Mr. Handy through Snip Snip, the Mr. Handy reprogrammed for organ harvesting, but they even see the origins of Fallout 4's infamous Codsworth Mr. Handy.\n\nThis is a great detail to include in the show, as it gives so much more depth to the character and hugely enhances world-building. By seeing Matt Berry's Sebastian Leslie, the character who, canonically, allowed his voice to be used in all Mr. Handy bots, interact with Howard Cooper, the series expands the franchise lore excitingly. Furthermore, the show did an incredible job at recreating the Mr. Handy bots in live action, with the game's designs being replicated perfectly, alongside their crude humor delivered in excited tones.\n\n4 Vault Boy Bobbleheads Are Absolutely Everywhere\n\nRelated\n\nEvery Fallout 4 Vault, Explained\n\nFallout 4 had some truly interesting Vaults and experiments to dive into and explore.\n\nFallout's biggest collectible by far is the Vault-Boy bobbleheads that can be found throughout the Wasteland in Fallout 3, 4, and 76, with each one granting players a single S.P.E.C.I.A.L. point. Hunting down collectibles is one of the most enjoyable components of any game, especially open-world ones like Fallout, giving gamers a reason to explore every inch of the map and rewarding them for doing so.\n\nJust like how collectibles are hidden throughout the recent Fallout games, countless Vault-Boy bobbleheads are hidden in the background of the show. This acts as a clear reference to the franchise's collectible bobbleheads and is a neat detail that further shows just how much care and respect went into the show's creation, and why it has earned its title as one of the best video game adaptations yet.\n\n3 Game-Accurate Pip-Boys\n\nAnother staple of the Fallout franchise is its trusty Pip-Boys, wearable devices that allow players to access their maps, inventories, health diagnostics, quests, S.P.E.C.I.A.L. skill tree, and numerous other functions. These Pip-Boys are essentially the post-apocalyptic version of smartphones, and without them, the average Vault Dweller would be lost and vulnerable in the Wasteland, and clueless in the Vault. Pip Boys are also great sources of entertainment, giving gamers the option to tune into 50s-era radio stations during their travels and play in-game video games when found in the Wasteland.\n\nIn the show, Lucy is equipped with her Pip-Boy along with the show's other Vault Dwellers, and these devices are game-accurate -- complete with all the same tabs from other Fallout games, like Stats (Statistics), Inv (Inventory), Data, Map, and Radio. Furthermore, the show offers fans a glimpse into Lucy's health statistics in Episode 3, which, just like in the recent games, shows the health of each individual limb with the classic Vault-Boy diagram. Just like the other aforementioned fantastic details, the game-accurate Pip-Boy increases immersion within the Fallout show and is great fan service.\n\n2 The Show Matches Fallout's Humor\n\nRelated\n\nWhere Every Fallout Entry Takes Place, Explained\n\nThe Fallout franchise takes place across the United States, showcasing how different groups adapted to the post-apocalyptic landscape.\n\nThe Fallout series is well-known for its satirical, sarcastic humor, and the show absolutely nails this, with fans praising the show's hilarious comedy aspects. Despite the world's tragic transformation into the Wasteland, and the dire situation most characters are in, the comedy truly works -- dark, monotone jokes are made in the bleakest of situations, a combination which rarely fails to get a laugh.\n\nElla Purnell (Lucy) and Aaron Moten (Maximus) effortlessly deliver some of the best lines in the show, really playing into Fallout's unique tone of comedy. As a Vault Dweller, Lucy's understanding of the world and social interactions is very limited, so her interactions with other characters are always funny and entertaining. This is once again another small detail that demonstrates the care and respect put into the show, all of which build a great adaptation.\n\n1 Vault-Tec's History Is Explored\n\nVault-Tec, the company behind the implementation of vaults across America in preparation for nuclear war, has appeared in every Fallout game, acting as the franchise's overarching antagonist. Much of their history has been a mystery, especially how they knew how and when to prepare for the bombs to drop. Furthermore, the evil corporation has been known to conduct disturbing experiments on humans in different vaults, adding to Fallout's dark lore.\n\nThe adaptation not only focuses on Vault-Tec as the primary antagonist but also reveals much more about their evil history, including a confirmation of something that many fans theorized about for years -- that the corporation was responsible for the destruction of Earth. The show heavily details how Vault-Tec brought about the end of the world and how they plan on controlling it, furthering the lore of the franchise. On top of this, fans discover the origins of Vault-Boy and the Vault-Tec colors. All of these details make this adaptation an important part of the Fallout franchise and prove why it is essential for fans of the games to invest in.\n\nFallout\n\nThe Fallout franchise, a hallmark of post-apocalyptic gaming, transports players to a retro-futuristic world devastated by nuclear war. Set in an alternate history where advanced technology and 1950s culture collide, the series begins in the year 2077, when nuclear bombs devastate the Earth. Survivors emerge from massive underground bunkers called Vaults to navigate the harsh wastelands, filled with mutants, raiders, and remnants of pre-war society.\n\nEach game in the series, from the original Fallout to the latest installment, presents a unique narrative centered around themes of survival, exploration, and moral ambiguity. Players often assume the role of a Vault Dweller or Wastelander, making crucial decisions that shape the fate of various factions and settlements. With its open-world design, intricate storytelling, and deep role-playing mechanics, Fallout has captivated audiences, offering a rich blend of action, strategy, and atmospheric storytelling that examines the enduring human spirit amidst desolation.\n\nCreated by Tim Cain , Leonard Boyarsky\n\nFirst TV Show Fallout\n\nFirst Episode Air Date April 10, 2024\n\nCast Ella Purnell , Aaron Moten , The weapon can theoretically solve the Commonwealth's water crisis and generate valuable purified water for trade. Introducing Thirst Zappers to settlers could revolutionize travel and trade in Fallout 4 , but water merchants may not be pleased with the competition.\n\nVeterans of Fallout 4's Nuka-World DLC will be more than familiar with one of the weapons it introduces, the Thirst Zapper. This weapon is a gift from Gage which allows the Sole Survivor to defeat the old Overboss despite being useless in terms of damage. However, its realpotential lies outside of combat.\n\nWhen the weapon is equipped or re-equipped, its ammo refills to maximum, giving it unlimited ammunition. Unlike most weapons, the Thirst Zapper does not shoot bullets or lasers, but water, which is highly desirable for every living thing, but especially for the residents of the Commonwealth. This means that giving every person a Thirst Zapper would ensure they never go thirsty again.\n\nFallout 4's Thirst Zapper Is A Strangely Useful Weapon\n\nAn Infinite Source Of Clean Water\n\nMost players will likely toss aside the Thirst Zapper after the \"Taken for a Ride\" quest due to its uselessness outside the Nuka-Cade. The branded squirt gun does, however, get much better if the Sole Survivor finds the Project Cobalt schematics, which were meant to turn any everyday item into a lethal weapon. After finding these schematics, the Thirst Zapper can become one of the most powerful weapons in Fallout 4, with a damage output which rivals the Fat Man mini-nuke launcher.\n\nShould the player avoid using these modifications, however, their weapon will be much more useful from a practical perspective. While the gameplay does not allow it to be used this way, realistically, people could fire the Zapper into bottles, watering cans, or directly onto withering crops. The animations do show a bottle of liquid being poured into the gun, but the 999 shots the player receives from a single bottle make it seem like the weapon is at least multiplying the water poured into it.\n\nProviding Infinite Water To Fallout 4's Thirsty Commonwealth\n\nThirst Zappers Could Solve The Wasteland's Water Crisis\n\nThere is great potential for a handheld, infinite water source to change the face of Fallout 4's Commonwealth. While the water crisis is not as dire as it was in Fallout 3's Capital Wasteland, many people still struggle to get water on a daily basis. Dialogue from Sturges during the \"Sanctuary\" side quest makes it clear that the fresh water running through the Commonwealth is still heavily irradiated. Water needs to be pumped from aquifers underground or highly purified to remove radiation and pathogens.\n\nThe value of water is further exemplified by its high value. Each can of purified water has a base value of 20 caps, and the player can exploit workshop mechanics to produce hundreds of cans. In fact, Fallout 4's best settlement locations can be set up to allow for potentially dozens of industrial water purifiers to be placed. Sheng Kowalski seems to be wise to the water-selling scheme, having monopolized Diamond City's sole reliable source of clean water, which the Sole Survivor can witness in a relatively hidden Fallout 4 quest, \"Pool Cleaning.\"\n\nThirst Zappers would all but remove the market demand for water from the Commonwealth's thirsty residents. Not only is it an infinite source of water, but it can be held in one hand, meaning it can be taken anywhere. Introducing Thirst Zappers could give settlers a greater ability to travel in Fallout 4, helping trade. However, water merchants like Sheng would certainly be displeased, having lost their captive audience.\n\nFallout 4\n\nBethesda's action RPG Fallout 4 puts players into the vault suit of the Lone Survivor, a pre-war soldier from an alternate future cryogenically frozen inside Vault 111. After their infant son is kidnapped, they venture out into the irradiated wasteland of the Commonwealth to scour the ruins of Boston for any sign of him. In doing so, they encounter various factions and companions and use an array of skills and abilities to navigate the apocalyptic remnants of society.\n\nRPG\n\nAction\n\nOpenCritic Top Critic {"uri": "2024-07-436136748", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-28", "time": "12:35:05", "dateTime": "2024-07-28T12:35:05Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-28T12:00:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.572549045085907, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-london-best-starting-traits-folon/", "title": "Fallout London: Best Traits", "body": "Fallout 4 Trick Helps You Get Best Power Armor in the Game Without Doing Its Quest\n\nQuick Links\n\nAcrobat\n\nChem Head\n\nClaustrophobic\n\nFour Eyes\n\nGifted\n\nHeavy Handed\n\nHoarder\n\nKamikaze\n\nNight Owl\n\nNumbskull\n\nPuritan\n\nSleepwalker\n\nFallout London is a total conversion mod for Fallout 4 that tells an entirely new story. Taking place sometime between Fallout 1 and Fallout 2, this game hops across the pond to tell a tale of the apocalypse in Old Blighty. Waking up in a mysterious laboratory, we customize our character under the careful watch of two scientists, before circumstances lead to our escape into the ruined streets of London.\n\nFallout London overhauls many of Fallout 4's mechanics while introducing some new ones. One of these new mechanics is the option of selecting Starting Traits when you make your character. These function near-identically to the traits from Fallout: New Vegas, allowing you to modify your starting character with traits that each provide a benefit and a drawback. This guide will break down the available options and discuss which ones are the most useful for certain builds.\n\nRelated\n\nHow to Play Fallout London on Steam & GOG\n\nFallout London is an amazing mod for Fallout 4, but it can be tricky to get working. Here's how to install and play the mod.\n\nAcrobat\n\nThe Acrobat Trait allows you to trade carry weight for speed, granting +10% Movement Speed but reducing your Carrying Capacity by 50lbs. This can be helpful if you're using melee weapons, so you can get in close more easily, but the loss of Carrying Capacity is a pretty huge tradeoff due to having less access to storage in the early stages of the game. If you can push through the early-game then this trait can be quite useful for ranging across London.\n\nChem Head\n\nChem Head gives -1 to all SPECIAL Stats whenever you aren't under the influence of Chems, forcing you to regularly dose up if you want to be at full strength. Thankfully, it also quadruples the duration of all Chems to make this easier and help you get more out of all your Chems. This Trait can be incredible if you can handle the penalty, especially if you have a high Intelligence Stat and the right Perks to craft your own Chems.\n\nClaustrophobic\n\nThis one's a tough recommendation. It gives you +1 to all SPECIAL stats when you're outdoors, in exchange for turning that into a -1 to all SPECIAL stats whenever you're indoors. Since decent chunks of the game take place inside buildings and London's Tube Network is extensive, this is likely a bad choice despite the theoretically huge buff.\n\nFour Eyes\n\nSimple and straightforward, Four Eyes gives you +1 Perception while wearing glasses and -1 Perception if you aren't. Once you grab some glasses, this is just free Perception, making this is an excellent pick for builds that focus on gunplay.\n\nGifted\n\nGifted makes leveling up harder by reducing exp gain by 15%, but in exchange, it increases all SPECIAL stats by 1. This is a massive boost early on, though naturally, the slower leveling can be a problem later on. Since Intelligence increases EXP earned, you'll be able to offset some of, if not all of, this penalty eventually.\n\nHeavy Handed\n\nThis Trait is great for melee builds if you aren't a fan of Power Attacks. It increases all Melee and Unarmed Damage by 20% but makes Power Attacks meaningless. Since Power Attacks are quite slow and can be interrupted easily, this is worth considering if you want to hit fast and hard.\n\nHoarder\n\nThis one is pretty much always a good pick. It gives you an extra 75lbs of Carrying Weight in exchange for dropping your movement speed to zero when you're over-encumbered. Running around while over-encumbered is never a good idea anyway, and the extra Carrying Weight will make it harder to hit your weight limit in the first place.\n\nKamikaze\n\nThe Trait of Choice for a Glass Cannon Build, Kamikaze regenerates your Action Points 50% faster in exchange for taking 20% more weapon damage. This makes it easier to sprint around, reposition, and use VATS to cripple enemy limbs in combat. If you're building a Sniper or any kind of ranged build, it shouldn't be too hard to mitigate that extra incoming damage by taking cover and playing a little defensively.\n\nNight Owl\n\nNight Owl is a Trait that, with a little planning, can be easily taken advantage of. It grants +1 to Perception and Intelligence at night, in exchange for penalizing both during the day. If you plan carefully and rest through the daytime, you can easily have the bonus anytime it matters.\n\nNumbskull\n\nA potentially powerful Trait that comes with a steep penalty. Numbskull gives you a permanent +1 bonus to Strength, Endurance, and Luck. In exchange, your Intelligence can never be raised above 3, making certain builds impossible. If you don't care about the Intelligence Stat, then this can be a good pick for getting some free bonus stats.\n\nPuritan\n\nThe Puritan Trait grants you +1 Strength and Endurance, helping you to hit harder, carry more, and giving you more HP to work with. The trade-off, however, is that using Chems or drinking Alcohol will reverse this bonus. The exceptions to this are Stimpacks, Rad-X, and Radaway, so you can still manage your health and deal with radiation, but you won't be able to use powerful drugs like Hero or take advantage of the buffs granted by alcohol without losing 1 Strength and 1 Endurance. If you're up to the challenge, this could still be a very nice bonus on builds using melee weapons, or just if you want extra carrying capacity and health.\n\nSleepwalker\n\nThe Sleepwalker Trait is a fun one, causing you to occasionally wake up in random places after sleeping. This can be amazing if you enjoy exploring and want to stumble across all kinds of random locations, but can also be troublesome if you decide to take a nap and end up somewhere you aren't prepared for. It's a pretty safe choice and can lead to some very interesting discoveries, but it's entirely down to personal taste. Much like Wild Wasteland in New Vegas, this can lead to some entertaining encounters.\n\nFallout 4\n\nRPG\n\nAction\n\nSystems\n\nOpenCritic Reviews Top Critic Rating:87/100 Critics Recommend:89%\n\nFranchise Fallout\n\nPlatform(s) PC , PS4 , PS5 , Xbox One , Xbox Series X , Xbox Series S\n\nReleased November 10, 2015\n\nDeveloper(s) Bethesda\n\nPublisher(s) Bethesda\n\nEngine {"uri": "2024-07-436386070", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-28", "time": "19:13:11", "dateTime": "2024-07-28T19:13:11Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-28T19:00:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5647059082984924, "url": "https://screenrant.com/fallout-4-unlock-university-credit-union-prototype-up77/", "title": "Fallout 4: How To Unlock The University Credit Union (Prototype UP77)", "body": "Fallout 4 Player Discovers A Horrifying Truth About A Common Wasteland Enemy\n\nWith so many weapons available in Fallout 4, many players seek a challenge to find an optimally performing option. The Prototype UP77 'Limitless Potential' stands among one of the most unique firearms, and as powerful as it is, it is equally challenging and somewhat tedious to look for.\n\nLocated within University Credit Union in Fallout 4, obtaining the weapon requires an awful lot of lockpicking and Terminal-hacking, which can be difficult if players aren't adequately leveled. To find and unlock The University Credit Union, bring yourself a bunch of Bobby Pins and get ready to do heaps of exploring.\n\nRelated\n\n8 Best Weapons In Fallout 4 (& How To Get Them)\n\nFallout 4 offers plenty of firearms and melee weapons, that come with legendary effects and can be further enhanced with mods for better utility.\n\nUniversity Point Location In Fallout 4\n\nSouthern-Central Region Of Commonwealth\n\nTo find the Prototype UP77 'Limitless Potential,' players must venture to a faction of the Institute, University Point Student Union, as it is locked in the Credit Union bank vault. This can be found in the Southern-Central region of the Commonwealth, specifically between Andrew Station and Neponset Park. Take a look at your Pip-Boy in Fallout 4 to find the most convenient fast-travel spots nearby.\n\nThere are two entrances to the union, with the public entrance identifiable with a 'Bank' sign outside, which is where players need to go. This will give you access to a small lobby separated from the back employee area. This segment is locked by a Terminal that players of Novice-level must hack into.\n\nWhen you approach the building, beware of the hostile Synths patrolling the area outside. When you enter the area, ensure you're ready for a fight and packed with ammo and consumables for survival.\n\nUpon taking care of the enemies, you can head indoors and make an immediate right to find the Terminal in Fallout 4. Use it to unlock the steel door blocking your path, allowing you to enter the building. Once you get through, head downstairs to find yourself inside the Student Credit Union.\n\nYou will find useful items, including a Bobby Pin Box, on the bottom shelf beneath the cashier machines in the Credit Union. This Box is especially useful when clearing out this building for items.\n\nHow To Unlock The University Credit Union Vault\n\nRequires Master-level Lockpicking\n\nHeading down the next set of stairs, open the Security Gate to find another Novice-level Terminal. This must be used to hack open the Credit Union bank vault in Fallout 4. Alternatively, those who want to save their Bobby Pins can access the vault by using Gerald's Vault Password.\n\nGerald's Vault Password can be found in the employee area, kitchen, and break room. As there are quite a few vaults and terminals within this building, Streamer House on YouTube recommends leveling up your lockpicking skills and getting the locksmith perk to ensure you don't miss out on any key items.\n\nWhen you unlock and enter the vault, you will find several safes, some already open, while others are broken. Among them, you will see a locked safe in the second row of the right-hand wall that requires Master-level lockpicking in Fallout 4.\n\nWithin the open and locked safes, a plethora of extra items are worth taking, including an Ammo Box containing Plasma Cartridges, Caliber, and Rounds. You can also pick up Nuka Cola, Rad-X, and several crafting materials. Two more locked Advanced-level and Master-level safes also contain ammunition and valuable materials.\n\nMaster-level is the highest-ranking lock in Fallout 4 and, therefore, the hardest to open. If you haven't leveled up this skill yet, you won't be able to use your Bobby Pins to open the safe. To bypass this issue, look for Campbell's Safe Password, which can be found in the student records terminal in Sedgwick Hall.\n\nSedgwick Hall is another Institute faction close by, within University Point. You can find the key card to open the Master-lock safe by heading through a broken wall hole within the main first-floor entrance. Players must go through the student records terminal in the mainframe and navigate through the necessary files, reaching the following entry, listed in order:\n\n'Student Directory for 2077-2078' > 'Enrolled Graduates' > 'G-M'\n\nTo obtain Campbell's Safe Password in Fallout 4 within this Terminal, players are required to first view the entries of the professor's terminal on the third floor before accessing the student records terminal.\n\nWhether you went to acquire the password or lockpicked your way into the Master-level safe on the second row, you will find a red button on the right side of the safe's interior. Press it to open a wall panel within the vault, allowing access to the secret neighboring lab.\n\nPrototype UP77 'Limitless Potential' Location & Stats\n\nWeapon Features & Abilities\n\nUpon entering, you will find the Prototype UP77 'Limitless Potential' on a large table in the center of the room, available to pick up. You will also conveniently find Fusion Cells surrounding the weapon and a few workbenches around the room. The Weapons Workbench will allow you to immediately customize and mod your newly acquired firearm if you wish.\n\nWeapon Features\n\nStats\n\nType\n\nUnique Energy weapon\n\nEffect\n\nUnlimited ammo capacity\n\nAmmo\n\nFusion Cell\n\nMagazine Size\n\nUnlimited\n\nFire Rate\n\n90\n\nRange\n\n227\n\nAccuracy\n\n96\n\nSell Value\n\n306 Caps\n\nOne of the unique features of the Prototype UP77 'Limitless Potential' weapon in Fallout 4 is that it possesses the Never Ending effect, which grants unlimited ammo capacity. This shouldn't be confused with having unlimited ammo, as it utilizes Fusion Cells, like other laser weapons found in the wasteland. Instead, it has an unrestricted Magazine, eliminating the need to reload when firing.\n\nNot only does this make you faster when dealing damage in combat, but it also means that players will never have to stop shooting to reload. Due to this feature, the weapon aids in survivability, as those brief pauses from reloading are usually when players become vulnerable and prone to being attacked by enemies in Fallout 4.\n\nSource: {"uri": "8250883357", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-30", "time": "15:04:03", "dateTime": "2024-07-30T15:04:03Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-30T15:03:21Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5529412031173706, "url": "https://gamingbolt.com/fallout-london-review-london-is-calling", "title": "Fallout: London Review - London is Calling", "body": "Fallout: London begins with the usual Fallout spiel - war unchanging, the world in ruins, etc. - but there's no Vault to emerge from. You don't venture into the wasteland to find a family member (thank heck), but rather answers and connections. The post-apocalyptic playground may still feature all the tenets of Fallout 4, from junk collecting and armor and weapon crafting to settlement building, but wrapped in the remnants of a completely different culture. London has fallen, and you have no idea who you are.\n\nAn amnesiac protagonist isn't a new concept, yet it remains a solid enough mechanic to introduce players to the world while allowing them to shape their own story. The lack of a voiced protagonist furthers that goal - for all intents and purposes, you're one of the people from the labs. Nothing is known about you or the scientists seemingly conducting experiments in a facility beneath The Shard. When a gang known as the Vagabonds breach it on an alleged supply run, you break free.\n\n\"It's amazing and - to employ a clich\u00e9 - really makes you feel like you've awakened in a retrofuturistic London that's gone to hell and back.\"\n\nSome tea bags, Radshrews and terminal digging later, and the only relevant name throughout it all is Smythe (Mr. or Mrs., depending on your gender). They don't seem all that hung up on you leaving - in fact, they subsequently unlock the doors, allowing you to take The Tube and escape. The journey doesn't last long, as it crashes onto the street, leaving you with afflictions resulting in less damage dealt and more taken. After a brief conversation with the same Vagabonds, it's time to cut loose.\n\nJoin up with the Peaky Blinders rejects and help them with their tasks, perhaps get some sweet weapons and clothes, or venture to the canned goods factory to locate the Thamesfolk. You can also reject both choices and explore, weaving in and out of the main quest as you please.\n\nCompared to Fallout 4 or many other open-world titles, Fallout: London doesn't immediately douse you in random occurrences and side quests. The overcast skies, incessant rain and minimal music lend a darker mood to it all. The meticulously detailed environment further adds to the immersion. You'll walk down the street and see wrecks of double-decker buses, maybe venture into the Fesco (clearly based on Tesco) to see what's available and encounter some Bloatflies. The radio offers a mix of intriguing beats when the soundtrack isn't offering dour chords during the silent moments and heart-thumping beats during combat.\n\nThere are still terminals to investigate and NPCs to converse with, but the world-building relies almost as much, if not more, on the decrepit streets and skeletal remains. It's amazing and - to employ a clich\u00e9 - really makes you feel like you've awakened in a retrofuturistic London that's gone to hell and back. This may not vibe with every kind of player out there, especially if they need a constant stream of activities on the map, or random occurrences to keep themselves occupied.\n\n\"The fact that certain decisions have proper consequences is another feather in the mod's cap, to say nothing of all the speech checks for adding some extra flair to your dialogue exchanges.\"\n\nSticking to a quest path is beneficial for those who want more consistent narrative beats, and Fallout: London delivers in that department as well. I chose to head to the canned goods factory and got caught up with the owner wanting a rebellious worker taken care of. After robbing the former blind, I did the deed, received some Tickets (the de facto currency), and hightailed it alongside my new dog, Churchill. We ventured to a checkpoint leading to Thameshaven, told that the front was barricaded, and proceeded through a series of irradiated underground tunnels that wouldn't be out of place in a Metro game.\n\nHelping the mutated Thamesfolk was key towards locating Archie, a boy who knew about the underground laboratories, and where we may potentially find another. First, a former Tommy conscript turned mercenary seeks to destroy some Mittenlurk nests before allowing me entry into the crashed plane to speak with Archie. What ensues is a game of \"the floor is lava\", navigating rooftops and makeshift walkways to avoid mega-radiated water, find the nests and destroy them.\n\nThroughout all this, Fallout: London is opening up to you through its characters about the state of its world and the different factions. The Vagabonds' leader Sebastian Gaunt is an ally of the Thamesfolk but is considered a wanted man by the Tommies. The Thamesfolk are sheltered and seemingly pitiful but also wary and passive-aggressive to outsiders.\n\nOther factions exist, each with dedicated quest chains, and it's a joy to slowly unravel this brutal world while coming to care about those within it. The fact that certain decisions have proper consequences is another feather in the mod's cap, to say nothing of all the speech checks for adding some extra flair to your dialogue exchanges. Unfortunately, the voice-acting ranges from decent to forgettable - it gets the job done, but very few performances stand out.\n\n\"Even if you can deal with all that, optimization remains one of the biggest hurdles to enjoying Fallout: London.\"\n\nHowever, it bears remembering that this is still Fallout 4's gameplay. The shooting mechanics and crafting are still very serviceable, but melee combat remains somewhat clunky. In a game that pushes for more of the latter, whether it's reserving ammunition for the harder-hitting foes or relying on knives in relatively close-quarters scenarios, it's rough.\n\nNot enough to make the game unplayable or outright annoying, but I lost count of all the times I tried to swing my knife again while my character was seemingly trapped in molasses, finishing the first attack. On the bright side, the selection of quirks at the beginning, allowing for further build specialization or just wacky fun, helped feed more into the role-playing.\n\nThe Fallout 4 base also means that despite excellent attention to detail, well-realized environments, and much more, the visuals remain several years behind some of today's best (or second-best). Even if you can deal with all that, optimization remains one of the biggest hurdles to enjoying Fallout: London. GOG is the best way to go, but even with a relatively smooth installation process, there are crashes galore. It starts when emerging from the Tube crash and continues, seemingly at random, regardless of what you do.\n\nInstalling another mod, Buffout 4, alongside some dependencies and a High FPS Physics Fix, resulted in a much more stable performance. However, the busier areas, whether it was the Thameshaven market or nighttime with lots of shadows and rain, resulted in severe FPS drops. Note that your mileage may vary and not in a good way - there are plenty who followed all the steps and tried other fixes, but still face crashes. Furthermore, the experience isn't bug-free, whether it's hands clipping through models, Churchill floating in the air when he's not blocking my path, etc.\n\n\"I feel excited to explore buildings, streets and locked doors - not for the XP, the loot or the materials, but to immerse myself further in this world and learn more about it.\"\n\nAt the end of the day, Fallout: London is a free mod with a scale rivaling many full-priced games. It offers tons of content, a compelling narrative with interesting characters and factions, and a stunningly realized world rife with detail. If Team FOLON can fix the various crashes and deliver more consistent performance, it's a worthy experience for any Fallout 4 fan (even if it doesn't revolutionize the well-worn gameplay). How long that may take and what it could break in the process is unknown.\n\nNevertheless, the current product is an enjoyable, solidly built experience. I feel excited to explore buildings, streets and locked doors - not for the XP, the loot or the materials, but to immerse myself further in this world and learn more about it.", "source": {"uri":
